
---

# 10\. Package Architecture

Affinity packs become optional modules.

```
Plain text

@salve/affinity-japan  
@salve/affinity-spain  
@salve/affinity-anime
```

Developers include only what they want.

---

# 11\. Developer API Example

```
TypeScript

const greeting \= salve.greet({  
  
  locale: "nl-BE",  
  
  affinities: \[  
    "japanese\_culture",  
    "spanish\_language"  
  \]  
  
})
```

Output:

```
Plain text

Goedemorgen  
  
Vandaag vieren ze Tanabata in Japan
```

---

# 12\. Why This Feature Is Actually Brilliant

It makes SALVE capable of:

-   cultural awareness
    
-   cultural curiosity
    
-   language learning
    
-   travel anticipation
    

without interfering with the core greeting logic.

It also opens the door to:

```
Plain text

education apps  
language apps  
travel apps
```

which could become **major adopters of SALVE**.

---

# 13\. Minimal v1 Implementation

This feature can actually be added cheaply:

1.  new `affinity` domain
    
2.  optional event packs
    
3.  low priority rule class
    

That's it.

No engine changes required.

---

# 14\. Long-Term Vision

With affinities SALVE becomes something bigger:

```
Plain text

A cultural calendar engine
```

not just a greeting generator.

---

If you want, I can also show you something extremely interesting:

**a unified SALVE context model**

because at the moment we have gradually introduced:

-   locale
    
-   religion
    
-   subculture
    
-   affiliation
    
-   affinity
    
-   relationship
    
-   formality
    

These can actually be reorganized into **a single elegant semantic context model**, which will make the engine much cleaner.

You: 

Please be my guest, do so.

ChatGPT: 

Below is a **unified, elegant SALVE context model** that cleanly organizes everything we’ve introduced—without turning the runtime into an unmaintainable bag of flags.

The trick is to separate:

1.  **Where the user is** (locale, timezone)
    
2.  **Who the user is** (person profile + addressability)
    
3.  **How the interaction is framed** (relationship, setting, formality)
    
4.  **Which calendars and conventions are active** (traditions, subcultures, affinities)
    
5.  **What the engine is allowed to do** (policy/safety)
    

This yields a context object that is:

-   language/culture agnostic
    
-   deterministic
    
-   extensible via plugins
    
-   safe (no inference)
    
-   CLDR-adjacent
    

---

## 1) SALVE Context v1

```
TypeScript

export interface SalveContextV1 {  
  // (A) Temporal & locale environment  
  env: {  
    now: Date;  
    timeZone?: string;            // IANA TZ if known  
    locale: string;               // BCP-47 input locale (user environment)  
    outputLocale?: string;        // BCP-47 output language for text (default: env.locale)  
    region?: string;              // ISO-3166-1 alpha-2 if known/derived  
  };  
  
  // (B) Interaction frame (how we’re speaking)  
  interaction: {  
    phase: "opening" | "closing";  
    setting: "ui" | "chat" | "email";  
    role?: "initiator" | "responder";  
  
    relationship?: "stranger" | "acquaintance" | "friend" | "family" | "superior" | "subordinate";  
    formality?: "formal" | "informal" | "neutral";  
  
    // style = rhetorical rendering, never inferred  
    style?: "neutral" | "formal" | "ceremonial" | "poetic" | "playful" | "archaic" | "liturgical" | "bureaucratic" | "minimal";  
  };  
  
  // (C) Person being addressed (the user / recipient)  
  person?: {  
    // naming  
    givenNames?: string\[\];        // user-entered  
    surname?: string;  
    preferredName?: string;       // optional display preference  
  
    // addressability signals  
    gender?: "male" | "female" | "nonbinary" | "unknown";  
    titles?: Array<{  
      system: "academic" | "civil" | "religious" | "military" | "other";  
      code: string;               // e.g. "dr", "prof", "judge"  
    }>;  
  
    // personal dates  
    birthday?: string;            // YYYY-MM-DD (optional)  
    nameday?: {  
      enabled?: boolean;          // user/dev flag  
      locale?: string;            // nameday tradition locale (e.g. "el-GR", "bg-BG")  
      saintIds?: string\[\];        // optional resolved canonical saint ids  
    };  
  };  
  
  // (D) Declared memberships (strong / identity-like)  
  // These influence core greeting choice, but MUST be explicitly provided.  
  memberships?: {  
    traditions?: string\[\];        // e.g. \["orthodox", "catholic", "muslim", "secular", "lutheran"\]  
    subcultures?: string\[\];       // e.g. \["student\_corporation", "socialist"\]  
  };  
  
  // (E) Declared affinities (weak / interest-like)  
  // These never override core greeting; they only add optional “extras”.  
  affinities?: {  
    locales?: string\[\];           // “I like/learn these locales” e.g. \["ja-JP", "es-ES"\]  
    tags?: string\[\];              // e.g. \["anime", "japanese\_culture", "spanish\_language"\]  
  };  
  
  // (F) Policy (what the engine is allowed to emit)  
  // Defaults chosen for safe, non-presumptive behavior.  
  policy?: {  
    // Domains permitted in main greeting selection  
    allowDomains?: Array<  
      "institutional" | "protocol" | "religious" | "personal" | "bank" | "civil" | "time" | "baseline"  
    >;  
  
    // Whether “extras” (affinity reminders) may be emitted  
    allowExtras?: boolean;  
  
    // Whether political/ideological protocol address terms are allowed  
    allowSubcultureAddressing?: boolean;  
  
    // Whether religiously-affiliated greetings are allowed unless traditions explicitly declare them  
    requireExplicitTraditionsForReligious?: boolean;  
  
    // Repetition control (per-user memory keys)  
    repetition?: {  
      windowedGreetings?: boolean;   // e.g. New Year / month start  
      maxSameRulePerDays?: number;   // e.g. 3  
    };  
  };  
}
```

---

## 2) Why This Structure Works

### Clear semantic boundaries

-   `env` = objective environment (safe to infer)
    
-   `interaction` = how the developer wants to speak (configured)
    
-   `person` = recipient profile (optional)
    
-   `memberships` = explicit identity-like declarations (never inferred)
    
-   `affinities` = interests (never override core greeting)
    
-   `policy` = explicit constraints (enterprise-safe)
    

This prevents the most common category error:

> “Because locale is Arabic, we assume Muslim.”  
> No: Muslim greetings require either `memberships.traditions` or an explicit policy override.

---

## 3) How the Engine Uses Each Block

### Event selection inputs

-   bank/civil events: from `env.locale`, `env.region`, `env.timeZone`
    
-   religious events: only if `memberships.traditions` contains relevant traditions (or policy allows)
    
-   personal events (birthday/nameday): from `person.*`
    
-   protocol events/terms: only if `memberships.subcultures` contains relevant values
    
-   affinity events: only if `affinities.*` present AND `policy.allowExtras=true`
    

### Rule selection filters

Rules match against:

-   `interaction.*` (phase, setting, formality, relationship, style)
    
-   `memberships.*`
    
-   event presence
    

---

## 4) Outputs Become Structured

Instead of just returning one string, return a structured result:

```
TypeScript

export interface SalveOutputV1 {  
  primary: {  
    text: string;  
    act: string;             // from ontology  
    eventId?: string;  
    ruleId: string;  
  };  
  
  extras?: Array<{  
    text: string;  
    eventId: string;  
    ruleId: string;  
    kind: "affinity" | "info";  
  }>;  
  
  trace?: {  
    candidates: Array<{ ruleId: string; tuple: Record<string, number\> }>;  
    usedEvents: string\[\];  
  };  
}
```

This supports your demo website perfectly:

-   big hero = `primary.text`
    
-   below = `extras[]`
    
-   dev panel = `trace`
    

---

## 5) Example Contexts

### A) Belgian Dutch user with Spanish affinity

```
Plain text

env.locale: nl-BE  
memberships.traditions: \["catholic","secular"\]  
affinities.locales: \["es-ES"\]  
policy.allowExtras: true
```

Primary greeting uses Belgian bank/civil + time-of-day.  
Extras may show: “Hoy es …” for Spanish events.

### B) Greek Orthodox user (namedays enabled)

```
Plain text

env.locale: el-GR  
memberships.traditions: \["orthodox"\]  
person.nameday.enabled: true  
person.givenNames: \["Giannis"\]
```

Nameday provider resolves saint id → injects `salve.event.personal.nameday` → “Χρόνια πολλά”.

### C) German corporate user (titles)

```
Plain text

env.locale: de-DE  
interaction.formality: formal  
person.titles: \[{ system:"academic", code:"dr" }\]  
person.surname: "Müller"
```

Composition yields: “Guten Morgen, Herr Doktor Müller”.

---

## 6) How This Supports “Feature Creep” Safely

Whenever you add new capability, it should land in exactly one place:

-   new calendar type → new provider emits events
    
-   new greeting conventions → new pack rules referencing those events
    
-   new user preference → new policy flag
    
-   new “interest reminders” → affinities + extras (never primary)
    

This prevents the model from becoming chaotic.

---

## 7) Minimal Defaults for Sloppy Developers

If a developer supplies only:

```
Plain text

env.now + env.locale
```

SALVE can still function:

-   `interaction`: defaults to `opening/ui/neutral/neutral style`
    
-   `policy`: defaults to safe mode:
    
    -   religious/protocol domains require explicit memberships
        
    -   extras disabled
        
-   `person`: omitted → no address
    

So output degrades to time-of-day + baseline greetings.

---

## 8) Immediate Next Step

If you want to lock this down formally, the next step would be:

1.  **JSON Schema for SalveContextV1** (so configs can be validated)
    
2.  **Policy defaults document** (RFC style) describing safe behavior
    
3.  **Context normalization algorithm** (derive region from locale, default outputLocale, etc.)
    

I can draft any of those next.

You: 

I'm most interested in the context normalization algorithm, so to indeed derive regions from locale, the default output locale, and so on.

ChatGPT: 

Designing a **context normalization algorithm** is exactly the right next step, because SALVE’s runtime should **never operate directly on raw user input**. Instead it should first construct a **normalized context** with deterministic defaults and derived values.

This layer acts like the **CLDR locale resolution algorithm**, but extended for greetings.

Below is a **complete SALVE Context Normalization Algorithm (SCNA)** suitable for the runtime.

---

# SALVE Context Normalization Algorithm (SCNA)

## Purpose

Convert incomplete or ambiguous developer input into a **fully normalized `SalveContext`** that the greeting engine can reliably use.

The algorithm must guarantee:

```
locale  
region  
outputLocale  
timezone  
phase  
setting  
formality  
style  
policy
```

always exist after normalization.

---

# Step 0 — Input

The developer provides a partial context.

Example minimal input:

```
Plain text

locale: nl  
now: 2027-05-01T09:30
```

Normalization fills in the rest.

---

# Step 1 — Normalize Locale

Input locale must follow **BCP-47**.

Examples:

```
nl  
nl-BE  
de  
de-AT  
el
```

### Algorithm

```
if locale missing:  
    locale = browser.language || "en"
```

Normalize case:

```
language lowercase  
region uppercase
```

Example:

```
nl-be → nl-BE
```

---

# Step 2 — Derive Region

Many locales omit region.

Example:

```
nl  
de  
es
```

SALVE must map language → **default region**.

Use a simple table.

Example mapping:

| Language | Default region |
| --- | --- |
| nl | NL |
| de | DE |
| el | GR |
| es | ES |
| fr | FR |
| en | US |
| pt | PT |
| ar | EG |

Algorithm:

```
if locale contains region:  
    region = locale.region  
else:  
    region = defaultRegionTable\[language\]
```

Example:

```
locale: nl → region NL  
locale: el → region GR
```

---

# Step 3 — Resolve Output Locale

SALVE separates:

```
input locale (environment)  
output locale (greeting language)
```

Default rule:

```
outputLocale = locale
```

However developers may override:

Example:

```
locale: nl-BE  
outputLocale: el-GR
```

Meaning:

```
user environment Belgium  
but greeting in Greek
```

Normalization rule:

```
if outputLocale undefined:  
    outputLocale = locale
```

Then perform BCP-47 normalization.

---

# Step 4 — Determine Timezone

Timezone can come from:

1.  developer input
    
2.  browser
    
3.  region default
    

Algorithm:

```
if env.timeZone exists:  
    use it  
  
else if Intl API available:  
    use Intl.DateTimeFormat().resolvedOptions().timeZone  
  
else:  
    fallbackTimezoneByRegion
```

Example region mapping:

| Region | TZ |
| --- | --- |
| NL | Europe/Amsterdam |
| BE | Europe/Brussels |
| GR | Europe/Athens |
| US | America/New\_York |

Timezone is critical for:

```
dayPeriod detection  
event provider resolution
```

---

# Step 5 — Normalize Date

If `now` missing:

```
now = new Date()
```

Ensure timezone applied.

Derived fields:

```
localDate  
localTime  
weekday  
dayOfYear  
month  
day
```

These are cached in normalized context.

---

# Step 6 — Compute Day Period

Greeting rules rely on day periods.

Example mapping:

| Period | Time |
| --- | --- |
| night | 00–05 |
| morning | 05–11 |
| midday | 11–14 |
| afternoon | 14–18 |
| evening | 18–22 |
| lateNight | 22–24 |

Algorithm:

```
dayPeriod = resolveDayPeriod(localTime)
```

Locale packs may override ranges.

Example:

Spanish:

```
mañana starts later
```

---

# Step 7 — Normalize Interaction Frame

Defaults:

```
phase = opening  
setting = ui  
relationship = stranger  
formality = neutral  
style = neutral  
role = initiator
```

Algorithm:

```
interaction.phase ??= "opening"  
interaction.setting ??= "ui"  
interaction.relationship ??= "stranger"  
interaction.formality ??= "neutral"  
interaction.style ??= "neutral"  
interaction.role ??= "initiator"
```

---

# Step 8 — Normalize Person Profile

If person exists:

### Given names

Normalize whitespace.

```
"  Jan  " → "Jan"
```

### Preferred name fallback

```
preferredName = first(givenNames)
```

### Gender

If missing:

```
gender = "unknown"
```

### Titles

Normalize codes.

Example:

```
Dr → dr  
Professor → prof
```

---

# Step 9 — Normalize Memberships

Ensure arrays exist.

```
memberships.traditions ??= \[\]  
memberships.subcultures ??= \[\]
```

Normalize values lowercase.

Example:

```
Orthodox → orthodox  
Muslim → muslim
```

---

# Step 10 — Normalize Affinities

Also arrays.

```
affinities.locales ??= \[\]  
affinities.tags ??= \[\]
```

Normalize BCP-47 for locale affinities.

Example:

```
es → es-ES
```

---

# Step 11 — Apply Policy Defaults

SALVE ships with safe defaults.

```
policy.allowDomains = \[  
  institutional,  
  time,  
  civil,  
  bank,  
  personal  
\]
```

Religious domain requires explicit tradition:

```
policy.requireExplicitTraditionsForReligious = true
```

Extras disabled by default:

```
policy.allowExtras = false
```

Subculture addressing disabled:

```
policy.allowSubcultureAddressing = false
```

---

# Step 12 — Generate Event Context

Once normalization is done:

Event providers run.

Providers receive:

```
region  
locale  
date  
memberships  
person
```

Providers emit events.

Example:

```
salve.event.bank.be.labour\_day  
salve.event.personal.nameday
```

---

# Step 13 — Final Normalized Context

Example output:

```
JSON

{  
  "env": {  
    "locale": "nl-BE",  
    "region": "BE",  
    "outputLocale": "nl-BE",  
    "timeZone": "Europe/Brussels",  
    "now": "2027-05-01T09:30:00"  
  },  
  
  "interaction": {  
    "phase": "opening",  
    "setting": "ui",  
    "relationship": "stranger",  
    "formality": "neutral",  
    "style": "neutral",  
    "role": "initiator"  
  },  
  
  "memberships": {  
    "traditions": \[\],  
    "subcultures": \[\]  
  },  
  
  "affinities": {  
    "locales": \[\],  
    "tags": \[\]  
  },  
  
  "policy": {  
    "allowExtras": false,  
    "allowSubcultureAddressing": false  
  }  
}
```

This object is now **safe for the rule engine**.

---

# Performance Considerations

Normalization must be extremely cheap.

Typical cost:

```
< 1 ms
```

Most work is simple lookups and string normalization.

---

# Determinism Guarantee

After normalization:

```
two identical contexts  
→ identical greeting output
```

This is crucial for reproducibility.

---

# Optional Future Enhancements

Future SALVE versions could extend normalization with:

### Locale fallback chains

Example:

```
nl-BE → nl → root
```

### CLDR region detection

IP or browser hints.

### Cultural inference (disabled by default)

Example:

```
Arabic locale → maybe Muslim
```

But only if explicitly allowed.

---

If you'd like, the **next piece that would make SALVE extremely robust** would be a **formal Greeting Resolution Pipeline diagram**, because after normalization the engine follows a very precise sequence of steps. This helps developers immediately understand the runtime architecture.

You: 

Okay, please do so, go ahead, but meanwhile, I also want to inject a remark having to do with the inference of gender from names. So you said if the gender is not explicitly provided, then no gender should be inferred, but I know it's maybe opening a can of worms with non-binary and gender issues in identity politics, but nonetheless, I think it might make sense to try and derive gender from a given name. So many names are gender-specific. Only a few names are shared between female and male, like Robin and Sam and so on. But if a user is called Jan or John or Yanis, we could safely assume that their gender is male. If a user is called Ioanna, Margaret, then we could safely assume that their gender is female. So before you go on and propose the formal greeting resolution pipeline diagram, I first want you to briefly comment on gender inference from given names.

ChatGPT: 

Your intuition is understandable and technically feasible, but in a system like **SALVE** the question is less *“can we infer gender?”* and more *“should the runtime depend on that inference?”*. The safest architecture is:

**Never treat inferred gender as authoritative**, but you *may* use it as a **low-confidence hint** when needed for grammar.

This keeps SALVE deterministic and culturally respectful while still allowing practical benefits.

---

# 1\. Why Gender Inference Is Technically Possible

Many languages have **highly gender-specific names**.

Examples:

| Name | Language | Likely gender |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Jan | Dutch/Polish | male |
| Giannis | Greek | male |
| Ioanna | Greek | female |
| Margaret | English | female |

Large datasets already exist:

-   **CLDR Person Name Data**
    
-   **US SSA name dataset**
    
-   **Wikidata given name gender properties**
    
-   **NamSor / Genderize datasets**
    

Accuracy for common names is often:

```
90–99%
```

---

# 2\. Why Direct Inference Is Dangerous

### A. Cultural ambiguity

Example:

| Name | Gender by culture |
| --- | --- |
| Andrea | male in Italy, female in US |
| Nikola | male in Balkans, female in Germany |

---

### B. Language grammar mismatches

Example:

German greeting:

```
Guten Morgen, Herr Müller
```

vs

```
Guten Morgen, Frau Müller
```

If SALVE guesses wrong, the greeting becomes awkward.

---

### C. Non-binary or personal identity cases

SALVE cannot know personal identity unless **explicitly provided**.

---

# 3\. Recommended SALVE Policy

Use **three gender states** internally:

```
explicit  
inferred  
unknown
```

Only **explicit** gender is trusted for strong grammatical decisions.

---

# 4\. Context Model Extension

Add gender source:

```
TypeScript

person: {  
  gender?: "male" | "female" | "nonbinary" | "unknown";  
  
  genderSource?: "explicit" | "inferred" | "unknown";  
}
```

---

# 5\. Gender Inference Algorithm

Only attempt inference if:

```
person.gender undefined  
AND givenNames present  
AND developer allows inference
```

Example policy flag:

```
TypeScript

policy.allowGenderInference?: boolean
```

Default:

```
false
```

---

### Step 1 — Normalize Name

```
"Giannis" → "giannis"
```

Remove accents optionally.

---

### Step 2 — Lookup Dataset

Dataset format:

```
JSON

{  
  "giannis": { "male": 0.99 },  
  "ioanna": { "female": 0.99 },  
  "robin": { "male": 0.55, "female": 0.45 }  
}
```

---

### Step 3 — Confidence Threshold

Example rule:

```
if probability >= 0.85  
  accept inference  
else  
  gender = unknown
```

---

### Step 4 — Mark as inferred

```
TypeScript

person.gender \= "male"  
person.genderSource \= "inferred"
```

---

# 6\. When SALVE May Use Inferred Gender

Safe uses:

### A. Optional address terms

```
Herr / Frau  
Mr / Ms  
Monsieur / Madame
```

but **only if developer allows it**.

---

### B. Grammatical agreement

Example languages:

Spanish

```
Bienvenido / Bienvenida
```

Greek

```
Καλωσόρισες / Καλωσόρισες
```

---

### C. Personal events

Nameday detection does **not** require gender.

---

# 7\. When SALVE Must Ignore Inferred Gender

Never use inferred gender for:

```
religious identity  
subculture identity  
titles  
protocol forms
```

Those require explicit data.

---

# 8\. Developer Control

Expose a configuration flag.

Example:

```
TypeScript

salve.configure({  
  genderInference: {  
    enabled: true,  
    dataset: "wikidata",  
    confidenceThreshold: 0.9  
  }  
})
```

Default behavior:

```
gender inference OFF
```

---

# 9\. Implementation Size

Gender inference can remain tiny.

Example dataset:

```
10–50k names  
≈ 200 KB JSON
```

Optional plugin:

```
@salve/provider-gender-names
```

---

# 10\. Why This Fits SALVE Philosophy

SALVE must remain:

```
deterministic  
culturally respectful  
non-presumptive
```

Using gender inference as **a hint rather than truth** preserves these goals.

---

# 11\. Practical Example

Input:

```
givenNames: \["Jan"\]  
gender: undefined  
policy.allowGenderInference: true
```

Inference:

```
gender = male  
source = inferred
```

Greeting rule:

```
Guten Morgen, Herr Jan Müller
```

If inference disabled:

```
Guten Morgen, Jan Müller
```

---

# 12\. Final Recommendation

SALVE should implement gender inference as:

```
optional plugin  
low confidence hint  
never mandatory
```

This gives developers flexibility without creating cultural or political problems.

---

If you like, the **next thing that would make SALVE extremely clear architecturally** is the **Greeting Resolution Pipeline**—a step-by-step diagram showing exactly how the engine moves from:

```
Raw context  
→ Normalized context  
→ Events  
→ Rule candidates  
→ Scoring  
→ Greeting output
```

This pipeline will basically be the **core runtime specification** of SALVE.

You: 

All right, thank you. So I agree with you on gender influence from names. It is indeed a useful addition if used carefully. So now, please go on with the greeting resolution pipeline, the step-by-step diagram.

ChatGPT: 

Below is the **SALVE Greeting Resolution Pipeline** as a **formal, step-by-step runtime diagram**. It’s written to be implementation-ready and to align with the schemas/ontology we defined.

I’m giving you:

1.  a **high-level block diagram**
    
2.  a **normative step sequence** (RFC-style MUST/SHOULD)
    
3.  the **data artifacts** produced at each stage (useful for dev-mode tracing)
    

---

## 1) High-Level Pipeline Diagram

```
Plain text

┌──────────────────────────────┐  
│  Input: Partial Context       │  
│  (developer + browser data)   │  
└──────────────┬───────────────┘  
               │  
               ▼  
┌──────────────────────────────┐  
│  (1) Context Normalization    │  
│  - normalize locale/timezone  │  
│  - derive region/outputLocale │  
│  - default interaction/policy │  
│  - optional gender inference  │  
└──────────────┬───────────────┘  
               │ NormalizedContext  
               ▼  
┌──────────────────────────────┐  
│  (2) Locale Fallback Chain    │  
│  - outputLocale chain         │  
│    e.g. nl-BE → nl → root     │  
└──────────────┬───────────────┘  
               │ LocaleChain  
               ▼  
┌──────────────────────────────┐  
│  (3) Event Collection         │  
│  - bank/civil holiday prov.   │  
│  - religious prov. (if allowed│  
│  - personal prov. (birthday,  │  
│    nameday)                   │  
│  - protocol prov. (if allowed)│  
│  - affinity prov. (extras only│  
└──────────────┬───────────────┘  
               │ ActiveEvents (+UpcomingEvents for demo)  
               ▼  
┌──────────────────────────────┐  
│  (4) Candidate Enumeration    │  
│  - load pack rules (locale &  │  
│    protocol packs)            │  
│  - filter by localeChain      │  
│  - filter by ontology fields  │  
│    (act/form/style/phase/etc) │  
│  - filter by events           │  
└──────────────┬───────────────┘  
               │ CandidateRules  
               ▼  
┌──────────────────────────────┐  
│  (5) Deterministic Scoring    │  
│  - compute ScoreTuple per rule│  
│  - apply policy constraints   │  
│  - apply repetition memory    │  
│  - stable tie-break           │  
└──────────────┬───────────────┘  
               │ WinnerRule (+RankedCandidates)  
               ▼  
┌──────────────────────────────┐  
│  (6) Address Resolution       │  
│  - institutional titles       │  
│  - protocol address forms     │  
│  - honorifics (if safe)       │  
│  - vocative name (locale)     │  
└──────────────┬───────────────┘  
               │ AddressParts  
               ▼  
┌──────────────────────────────┐  
│  (7) Style Rendering          │  
│  - style pack transform OR    │  
│    style-variant rule chosen  │  
│  - style fallback             │  
└──────────────┬───────────────┘  
               │ RenderPlan  
               ▼  
┌──────────────────────────────┐  
│  (8) Composition & Output     │  
│  - apply form patterns        │  
│    (ui/chat/email)            │  
│  - punctuation conventions    │  
│  - return primary + extras    │  
│  - emit trace                 │  
└──────────────────────────────┘
```

---

## 2) Normative Step Sequence (RFC-Style)

### (1) Context Normalization

-   The runtime **MUST** normalize `env.locale` to canonical BCP-47 casing.
    
-   The runtime **MUST** derive `env.region` if absent using a deterministic language→default-region map.
    
-   The runtime **MUST** set `env.outputLocale = env.outputLocale ?? env.locale`.
    
-   The runtime **MUST** set interaction defaults (`phase=opening`, `setting=ui`, `style=neutral`, etc.) if absent.
    
-   The runtime **MUST** set safe policy defaults if absent.
    
-   The runtime **MAY** infer gender from given names **ONLY IF** `policy.allowGenderInference=true`, and must mark it as `genderSource="inferred"`.
    

**Artifact:** `NormalizedContext`

---

### (2) Locale Fallback Chain

-   The runtime **MUST** compute a fallback chain from `env.outputLocale`.
    
-   The chain **MUST** end in `root`.
    

Example:

```
Plain text

el-GR → el → root  
nl-BE → nl → root
```

**Artifact:** `LocaleChain[]`

---

### (3) Event Collection

-   The runtime **MUST** invoke enabled event providers over the time window needed:
    
    -   **active window**: `now` (for greeting selection)
        
    -   **timeline window** (optional): `now → now + N days` (for demo/UX)
        
-   The runtime **MUST** apply policy gates:
    
    -   If `policy.requireExplicitTraditionsForReligious=true`, religious providers **MUST NOT** run unless a matching tradition is present in `memberships.traditions`.
        
    -   Protocol providers **MUST NOT** run unless `policy.allowSubcultureAddressing=true` AND subculture triggers exist.
        
    -   Affinity providers **MUST NOT** affect primary greeting selection; they may only populate `extras`.
        

**Artifact:** `ActiveEvents[]`, optionally `UpcomingEvents[]`

---

### (4) Candidate Enumeration

-   The runtime **MUST** load greeting rules from:
    
    -   all active `pack.locale`
        
    -   all active `pack.protocol` (only if triggers satisfied)
        
-   The runtime **MUST** filter rules by:
    
    -   locale membership in `LocaleChain`
        
    -   `interaction.phase` compatibility (e.g., valediction requires closing)
        
    -   `interaction.setting`, `interaction.formality`, `interaction.relationship` if specified in rule
        
    -   `style` if rule is style-specific (or later style layer handles it)
        
    -   `eventRef` presence in `ActiveEvents` if rule specifies one
        

**Artifact:** `CandidateRules[]`

---

### (5) Deterministic Scoring & Selection

-   For each candidate, the runtime **MUST** compute a score tuple and apply a total ordering.
    
-   The runtime **MUST** apply stable tie-breakers using `(packId, ruleId)`.
    
-   The runtime **MUST** enforce repetition constraints if enabled.
    

**Artifact:** `RankedCandidates[]`, `WinnerRule`

---

### (6) Address Resolution

-   The runtime **MUST** compute address parts separately from greeting selection.
    
-   Address selection **MUST** respect:
    
    -   `person.titles` (institutional)
        
    -   protocol address forms (only if triggered)
        
    -   locale honorific rules (only if enough data; inferred gender MAY be used only if policy allows)
        
    -   locale-specific vocatives (Greek vocative transforms, if configured)
        
-   If insufficient data exists (e.g., no surname for “Herr Doktor”), the engine **MUST** degrade gracefully by omitting the missing part.
    

**Artifact:** `AddressParts`

---

### (7) Style Rendering

Two valid strategies (both allowed):

-   **Variant rules**: locale packs contain explicit variants by `style`.
    
-   **Transform packs**: `pack.style` transforms base outputs.
    

The runtime **MUST** support neutral fallback:

```
Plain text

requested style → fallback chain → neutral
```

**Artifact:** `RenderedGreetingText` (and optionally `ExpectedResponseText`)

---

### (8) Composition & Output

-   The runtime **MUST** apply composition patterns based on `form` and `interaction.setting`.
    
-   The runtime **MUST** return a structured output:
    
    -   `primary.text`
        
    -   optional `extras[]` (affinity reminders, “today in X culture…”)
        
    -   optional `trace` (dev mode)
        

**Artifact:** `SalveOutputV1`

---

## 3) Step Artifacts for Developer Mode

This is what your demo page’s “developer panel” should show:

1.  **Normalized Context**
    
2.  **LocaleChain**
    
3.  **ActiveEvents / UpcomingEvents**
    
4.  **CandidateRules (filtered)**
    
5.  **RankedCandidates with ScoreTuple**
    
6.  **WinnerRule**
    
7.  **AddressParts**
    
8.  **Rendered Output**
    

---

## 4) Minimal Score Tuple (v1) vs Full Score Tuple (vNext)

### Minimal (v1)

```
Plain text

(  
  DomainRank,  
  EventRank,  
  PackPrecedence,  
  RulePriority,  
  LocaleMatchScore,  
  StableTieBreak  
)
```

### Full (later)

Adds:

```
Plain text

SpecificityScore,  
SettingMatchScore,  
FormalityMatchScore,  
RelationshipMatchScore,  
WindowFreshnessScore,  
StyleMatchScore
```

This makes v1 feasible without sacrificing determinism.

---

## 5) Example Walkthrough

Context:

```
Plain text

env.outputLocale = nl-BE  
now = 2027-05-01 09:30 Europe/Brussels  
style = ceremonial
```

Providers emit:

```
Plain text

salve.event.bank.be.labour\_day
```

Candidates:

-   `nl.labour_day.ceremonial` (domain=bank, style=ceremonial)
    
-   `nl.goedemorgen` (domain=time)
    

DomainRank(bank) > DomainRank(time) ⇒ holiday greeting wins.

Output:

```
Plain text

Een mooie Dag van de Arbeid gewenst
```
